  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26dc0c52-2d2b-4b95-bad9-f605385ed886'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2363263848981086007">The first collection of stories Stephen King has published since <i>Nightmares & Dreamscapes</i> nine years ago, <i>Everything's Eventual</i> includes one O. Henry Prize winner, two other award winners, four stories published by <i>The New Yorker,</i> and "Riding the Bullet," King's original e-book, which attracted over half a million online readers and became the most famous short story of th</span>
  <span id="freeText2363263848981086007" style="display:none">The first collection of stories Stephen King has published since <i>Nightmares &amp; Dreamscapes</i> nine years ago, <i>Everything's Eventual</i> includes one O. Henry Prize winner, two other award winners, four stories published by <i>The New Yorker,</i> and "Riding the Bullet," King's original e-book, which attracted over half a million online readers and became the most famous short story of the decade. <p> "Riding the Bullet," published here on paper for the first time, is the story of Alan Parker, who's hitchhiking to see his dying mother but takes the wrong ride, farther than he ever intended. In "Lunch at the Gotham Café," a sparring couple's contentious lunch turns very, very bloody when the maître d' gets out of sorts. "1408," the audio story in print for the first time, is about a successful writer whose specialty is "Ten Nights in Ten Haunted Graveyards" or "Ten Nights in Ten Haunted Houses," and though Room 1408 at the Dolphin Hotel doesn't kill him, he won't be writing about ghosts anymore. And in "That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is In French," terror is déjà vu at 16,000 feet. </p><p> Whether writing about encounters with the dead, the near dead, or about the mundane dreads of life, from quitting smoking to yard sales, Stephen King is at the top of his form in the fourteen dark tales assembled in <i>Everything's Eventual.</i> Intense, eerie, and instantly compelling, they announce the stunningly fertile imagination of perhaps the greatest storyteller of our time.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="2363263848981086007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2643024151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643024151" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643024151?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643024151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7326666794731911050">This is a reread for me, I first read this collection sometime back in the mid-2000’s. I just read “Elevation” by SK, and it left me a little unsatisfied and wanting more of King’s magic. I wasn’t ready to take on a full novel, so I grabbed this thinking I would just read a short story or two. Well, the next thing you know, I’ve finished the whole thing. “Everything’s Eventual” is a collection of 14 stories, or as the title states, 14 dark tales that I believe King wrote mostly in the 1990’s. I </span>
  <span id="freeText7326666794731911050" style="display:none">This is a reread for me, I first read this collection sometime back in the mid-2000’s. I just read “Elevation” by SK, and it left me a little unsatisfied and wanting more of King’s magic. I wasn’t ready to take on a full novel, so I grabbed this thinking I would just read a short story or two. Well, the next thing you know, I’ve finished the whole thing. “Everything’s Eventual” is a collection of 14 stories, or as the title states, 14 dark tales that I believe King wrote mostly in the 1990’s. I always enjoy King’s explanatory notes included with his short stories that often reveal his inspiration or parts of his process.<br /><br />This collection certainly filled the void that reading Elevation left. I think what really struck me about this group of stories is the honesty that King reveals. The stories hit on marriage, mother &amp; son relationships, divorce, and other relationships that King has clearly torn pieces from his past and laid bare for us to examine. Of course, they are all encapsulated in supernatural or horror stories. In two of the stories, “1408” and “The Road Virus Heads North”, King uses main characters that are writers, which is not unusual for him. But, continuing the theme of honesty, I feel like he opens the kimono here concerning his insecurities as a writer. In both stories the writers are horror authors and King uses phrases like “bottom feeders” or “projectile vomiting” to describe their genre and style. I think King did experience some self-doubt back in the ‘90s and it bleeds through here in his stories. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the title story, “Everything’s Eventual”. The main character, Dinky, reminds me a bit of Arnie from “Christine”, but the storyline harkens to “Hearts in Atlantis” and the Dark Tower series. I love the way King sets up some very unusual plot points and then slowly reveals the fantastic, weird backstory, like a strip tease. <br /><br />You also get a Roland of Gilead (Dark Tower) story, that’s not crucial for the Dark Tower storyline, but is essential if you’re a big fan of the series. The winner of the O. Henry short story competition, “The Man in the Black Suit” is included and is an excellent creepy fireside story. And “Riding the Bullet” was an early ebook that sold a half million and helped establish that format. <br /><br />All-in-all, a very strong assemblage of shadowy tales, some clever, some brilliantly horrific, but all engaging and authentically told.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7326666794731911050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2015602976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015602976" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015602976?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743235150" href="/book/show/644172.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015602976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5438356483476278138"><i>Everything’s Eventual</i> offers a mixed bag of short stories, fourteen tales that range from the horrifying to the mundane, each of which includes commentary from the author. <br/><br/>“Autopsy Room Four” explores the frightful prospect of premature burial. Comedic and tense, this is arguably the best story in the entire collection. <br/><br/>In “The Man in the Black Suit,” an old man recalls a chance encounter from his childhood that’s haunted him all his life. King plays to his strengths in this one, dabbling in the</span>
  <span id="freeText5438356483476278138" style="display:none"><i>Everything’s Eventual</i> offers a mixed bag of short stories, fourteen tales that range from the horrifying to the mundane, each of which includes commentary from the author. <br /><br />“Autopsy Room Four” explores the frightful prospect of premature burial. Comedic and tense, this is arguably the best story in the entire collection. <br /><br />In “The Man in the Black Suit,” an old man recalls a chance encounter from his childhood that’s haunted him all his life. King plays to his strengths in this one, dabbling in the realm of shadowy figures and terrifying monsters. <br /><br />“All That You Love Will Be Carried Away” is an inconclusive tale of a man with a penchant for collecting rest-area bathroom graffiti who suffers from a waning interest in being alive. King explains that he was encouraged by Bill Buford of <i>The New Yorker</i> to keep the ending ambiguous, and both Buford and King believe that decision strengthened the story. Whether or not that’s true is subjective. <br /><br />Bullets fly in “The Death of Jack Hamilton,” a story of Depression-era outlaws going head to head with the cops that will likely appeal to fans of car chases, westerns, or John Dillinger. <br /><br />“In the Deathroom” sees an American newspaper reporter interrogated in South America. The reporter must find a way to turn the tides if he wants to get out of the room alive. Labeled by King as “<i>Kafka-esque</i>,” this story investigates an unorthodox “what if” scenario to satisfying effect. <br /><br /><i>The Little Sisters of Eluria</i> is a fantasy novella about Roland Deschain of Gilead (from the Dark Tower series) in which Deschain crosses paths with some cunning women who are more than the doting caretakers they appear to be at first glance. King rightly states that “<i>you don’t need to have read the Dark Tower novels</i>” to enjoy this novella. <br /><br />The book’s namesake, “Everything’s Eventual,” reveals why nineteen-year-old Dink Earnshaw grinds paper in the garbage disposal and drops change down the storm-drain every week. Based on an image that randomly popped into King’s head, this story demonstrates his ability to take an idea and use it to craft an intriguing story that gives meaning to an imaginary character’s odd behavior. <br /><br />“L.T.’s Theory of Pets” introduces a disgruntled couple who gift each other a pet that bonds with the person who bought them, rather than the person they were gifted to. Intended to soften their discord, the gifted pets instead exacerbate their owners’ troubled relationship. King toys with his readers’ emotions in this one, tugging on heartstrings before throwing in a shocking twist. <br /><br />King once again romps through the realm of horror in “The Road Virus Heads North,” a gruesome tale about an unwitting man who acquires an eerie painting that seems to continually change in subtle yet grim ways. <br /><br />Amidst an argument over divorce papers, lunch takes an unexpected, violent turn in “Lunch at Gotham Café.” Though this reads like classic King, the plot twist feels clunky and forced. <br /><br />King conveys his idea of Hell in “That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is in French” – an intentionally repetitive story of <i>déjà vu</i>. <br /><br />“1408” takes a stab at being a supernatural tale of a haunted hotel room and succeeds marvelously. Coming in at a close second for best story in the collection, this shudder-inducing tale of a room on the thirteenth floor (whose room number totals thirteen) starts strong and continues to get better and better. <br /><br /><i>Riding the Bullet</i> is a novella that was first published as an e-book in 2000 to great acclaim, but King questions if the novella did well because of its content or because of the “<i>novelty of the electronic package</i>.” It’s reminiscent of an R.L. Stine book (i.e. creepy in a kitschy way), but underneath the surface it’s about the author grappling with the harsh reality that death eventually finds our loved ones. <br /><br />In “Luckey Quarter,” a hotel cleaning woman finds a lone quarter in her tip jar along with a note that reads, “<i>This is a luckey quarter! It’s true! Luckey you</i>!” If her premonition about the coin is correct, she may indeed by a fortunate woman. <br /><br />Given its absence of a running theme and the way the book deviates from a particular genre, <i>Everything’s Eventual</i> is a meandering collection of stories. Some satiate while others feel out of place, making for a relatively engaging but ultimately inconsequential read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5438356483476278138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2352703728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352703728" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352703728?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743235150" href="/book/show/644172.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352703728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17758797887256855221">"I want to make you laugh or cry when you read a story... or do both at the same time. I want your heart, in other words. If you want to learn something, go to school."<br/><br/>14 dark tales from the Master of Horror. From a serious case of deja-vu 16,000 feet in the air to a moving picture that becomes deadly, King delivers stories brimming with imagination and terror.<br/><br/>Overall, this collection was a winner for me! However, it does not surpass Night Shift - that one is pretty hard to beat, in my opinion. </span>
  <span id="freeText17758797887256855221" style="display:none">"I want to make you laugh or cry when you read a story... or do both at the same time. I want your heart, in other words. If you want to learn something, go to school."<br /><br />14 dark tales from the Master of Horror. From a serious case of deja-vu 16,000 feet in the air to a moving picture that becomes deadly, King delivers stories brimming with imagination and terror.<br /><br />Overall, this collection was a winner for me! However, it does not surpass Night Shift - that one is pretty hard to beat, in my opinion. I thought it would be easiest if I just gave a quick overview for my thoughts on each story as there was only 14 in this collection. Nearly all of the stories got 4 or 5 stars from me - only two failed to meet the mark!<br /><br />Autopsy Room 4 - really great story that made me feel quite claustrophobic and panicked. Loved the ending in particular!! Trust King to come up with that (excuse the pun)! 4.5 stars<br /><br />The Man in the Black Suit - a lot of people had said how scary this one was, but unfortunately I did not find it scary at all *sad face*, however I still enjoyed the story and execution! A memorable King short. 4 stars<br /><br />All That You Love Will Be Carried Away - a surprisingly emotional one that made me feel my feelings... one of those stories that really makes you think and will stay with you long after you put down the book. 4.5 stars<br /><br />The Death of Jack Hamilton - when I started this one I really didn't think I'd like it, but ended up enjoying it a lot more than I anticipated. A nice surprise! 4 stars<br /><br />In the Death Room - probably my least favourite in the collection, just fell a little flat for me. No doubt I'll forget about this one pretty quickly! 3.5 stars<br /><br />The Little Sisters of Eluria - well... I was always going to love this one (I can be honest when it comes to me being a bit biased...). It was AMAZING to be back with Roland in Mid-World, the little references to characters like Cort and Susan had me fangirling, as did all the usual Mid-World dialogue. The story was very compelling as a standalone and I was left wanting more! 5 stars<br /><br />Everything's Eventual - again, a heavily linked Dark Tower story with the inclusion of Dinky Earnshaw, and again, really really enjoyable. 5 stars<br /><br />LT's Theory of Pets - this was one of my favourites in the collection! I don't really laugh out loud that often when I read, but King has a way of tickling my funny bone and this one had me chuckling along. Then towards the end he starts toying with my emotions out of nowhere!! 5 stars<br /><br />The Road Virus Heads North - quite a creepy and unsettling story. Would put me off buying anything from a yard sale. Loved it!! 5 stars<br /><br />Lunch at the Gotham Cafe - this one was pretty crazy and made me feel pretty nervous. Sometimes if I imagine these things happening in real life it just sets me on edge. Situations like this are my worst nightmare - to be trapped somewhere with a complete psycho! *shivers* 4 stars<br /><br />That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is in French - King is right, hell is some form of repetition. This story was terrifying in its own way! 4 stars<br /><br />1408 - one of my most anticipated stories in this collection as the movie is quite popular (I haven't watched it yet, but now I can!). To be honest, I felt a little disappointed by it? It started out quite well and the premise was intriguing, but really didn't go down the route I expected and just wasn't scary like I hoped it would be. Still a good story, but I just wanted more. 4 stars<br /><br />Riding the Bullet - another one of my favourites in the collection. It was surprisingly emotional for me - I don't know, it was just pushing a lot of my triggers. I guess King's introduction about how it was related to his mother's death just made me view it in a different way. Loved this one! 5 stars<br /><br />Luckey Quarter - again, not the best story, pretty forgettable, but it wasn't terrible either! 3.5 stars<br /><br />So that's my King for the month! I might actually end up reading two King's in May, since we have the release of The Outsider to look forward to at the end of the month. How exciting! Overall, I'd give Everything's Eventual 4.5 stars out of 5. A really solid collection, I was impressed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17758797887256855221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_14830243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14830243" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14830243?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743235150" href="/book/show/644172.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2017-books">2017-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14830243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7160707781087720049">The wife had me watch 1408 a while back. I remembered it was in this collection but the only stories I even vaguely remember are the titular one and Little Sisters of Eluria. I figured 2017 was as good a time as any for a reread.<br/><br/>Even though I've been a Constant Reader for twenty years now, I always forget just how good Stephen King is at what he does until I start reading. The man knows his way around a story, though he gets a little wordy at times.<br/><br/>Like all short story collections, the stories v</span>
  <span id="freeText7160707781087720049" style="display:none">The wife had me watch 1408 a while back. I remembered it was in this collection but the only stories I even vaguely remember are the titular one and Little Sisters of Eluria. I figured 2017 was as good a time as any for a reread.<br /><br />Even though I've been a Constant Reader for twenty years now, I always forget just how good Stephen King is at what he does until I start reading. The man knows his way around a story, though he gets a little wordy at times.<br /><br />Like all short story collections, the stories vary in quality. I was surprised at how much I'd forgotten since I originally read this in 2002. Little Sisters of Eluria was better than I remembered, though Roland's story is missing something without the rest of the ka-tet. Everything's Eventual was great but since I came to it with more experienced eyes, it somewhat reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/698034.Time_Out_of_Joint" title="Time Out of Joint by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Time Out of Joint</a>. Autopsy Room was another great one. I liked The Road Virus Heads North but I feel like I read something similar a long time ago.<br /><br />Some of the stories seemed a little out of place. I wasn't enamored with LT's Theory of Pets, The Death Room, or The Death of Jack Hamilton. As for 1408, the story that prompted me to pick the book back up... I actually preferred the movie. It was an okay story about a hotel room haunted by something but the movie really fleshed things out. Also, the Mike Enslin in the book is couple notches higher on the douche scale than the one John Cusack plays in the movie.<br /><br />As with all short story collections, this one is a little hard to rate. Do Everything's Eventual, Little Sisters of Eluria, and Autopsy Room overcome the drag factor of the stories I didn't care that much for? At the end of the day, I'm slapping the traditional safety rating on this one. Three out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7160707781087720049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1486229636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1486229636" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1486229636?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer8687874561361031071"><b>
  <i>"Yet for me, there are few pleasures so excellent as sitting in my favorite chair on a cold night with a hot cup of tea, listening to the wind outside and reading a good story which I can complete in a single sitting."<br/>Stephen King, from his introduction</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>I genuinely looked forward to reading one of these tales each day, and that's the highest praise I can give a collection of short stories.</span>

<div id="review_600511937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600511937" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600511937?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600511937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18436472901056651063">As with all of Stephen King’s collections, I’m giving each story a one-sentence review. Before we begin, I would like to say a few things that have little to do with this book’s contents. If you do not care for personal stories in reviews, you should take this chance to move along, or you may scroll past the next few paragraphs. But I hope you’ll join me. Maybe my story will help someone who doesn’t know they need help.<br/><br/>While listening to this one (I chose the audiobook for this reread), I tried </span>
  <span id="freeText18436472901056651063" style="display:none">As with all of Stephen King’s collections, I’m giving each story a one-sentence review. Before we begin, I would like to say a few things that have little to do with this book’s contents. If you do not care for personal stories in reviews, you should take this chance to move along, or you may scroll past the next few paragraphs. But I hope you’ll join me. Maybe my story will help someone who doesn’t know they need help.<br /><br />While listening to this one (I chose the audiobook for this reread), I tried to remember what was going on in my life when this book came out. The year was 2002, the month was March, and six months prior, I had met the woman who would become my wife. I was working as a CNA for a local hospital and had been clean for about five months. My drug of choice was heroin. My wife is the reason I decided on recovery. Not because it was love at first site, or any of that nonsense, but because I finally found something I cared more for than the drugs. To this day, she doesn’t knows how bad I was. She might have an idea that I was on something, but I don’t think she knew the extent of my addiction.<br /><br />Any junkie will tell you, “Once a junkie, always a junkie.” As far as I see it, there are three stages of being a Junkie: Active junkie, relapsed junkie, and recovering junkie. There is no former junkie. If you’ve ever enjoyed hard drugs, you will always have a taste for it. The fits and seizures and sweats and vomiting everything you eat lasts about two weeks. If you’re lucky, you can sleep through the first few days. If you’re unlucky, like I was, you ride that motherfucker until sparks spit from the undercarriage. It’s a perpetual feeling of being dragged through a field of insulation. You can’t scratch deep enough and motor control is a concept lost on you. All this to kick something that makes you feel like you’re soaking in a warm cloud of perpetual orgasm whenever you take it. Is it any wonder junkies relapse? What most junkies don’t tell you is how badly you <i>need</i> a smoke, a shot, a snort, a drink, or whatever, for as long as one year later. That need eventually turns into a lesser want after the first year and you just have to ignore it if you’re going to make it. But that first year, man… It is fucking awful. Everything seems like it would be so much better if you relapsed, if you just gave in and took that smoke, that shot, that snort, that drink… But it won’t be. Sure, that first hour is gonna be magic, kid, but everything after is gonna feel like prematurely ejaculating inside the girl of your dreams, or having the man of your dreams squirt off after two pumps. You’ll want to go again. But you shouldn’t. Because getting better starts with changing your attitude and finding something greater than the addiction. <br /><br />But anyway. My recovery was why I hated this book when it first came out. I was in a bad place with a great person. And what I once considered one of King’s worst books turned out to be not so bad after all. I really enjoyed myself this time around. However, I still believe this is his weakest collection. Even if there are two amazing stories herein, the rest are just so-so. Here’s why:<br /><br />“Autopsy Room Four” – There’s a fine line between tribute and thievery, and King walks it in this homage to an old Twilight Zone episode. ***<br /><br />“The Man in the Black Hat” – King won an O. Henry award for this short, but other than the description of the titular devil, it falls a little flat for me. ***<br /><br />“All That You Love Will Be Carried Away” - This literary tale is, I think, what sets King apart from every other writer in the business - he can play at any genre and succeed because he’s a jack of all trade of the wordsmith variety. ****<br /><br />“The Death of Jack Hamilton” – Loved the disgusting bits, but this one goes on way too long. **<br /><br />“In The Deathroom” – I feel the same way about this one as I did with the last one. **<br /><br />“The Little Sister of Eluria” – Whether it be a day trip or a long vacation, Mid-World is one of my favorite destinations. ****<br /><br />“Everything’s Eventual” – A little tale of psychic persuasion with ambiguous morals. ***<br /><br />“L.T.’s Theory of Pets” – Just fucking funny. *****<br /><br />“The Road Virus Heads North” Can’t be bothered to give a fuck for this one, but the television adaptation wasn’t bad. *<br /><br />“Lunch at the Gotham Café” – So much gory fun. ****<br /><br />“That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is in French” – Repetitive to the point of inducing sleep, and unfortunately, that’s the point. **<br /><br />“1408” – Probably one of the coolest ideas King’s approached. ****<br /><br />“Riding the Bullet” – A fun little ride, but not much else. ***<br /><br />“Lucky Quarter” – Sad. ***<br /><br />In summation: <i>Everything’s Eventual</i> is King’s most inconsistent collection. You can almost hear King singing, “Somma dis shit, somma dat shit, a whole lotta uddah shit,” over and over as he threw these stories together. For my money, I would have loved to have seen him hold onto these and pair them with the tales in <i>Just After Sunset</i> and given us another massive collection like <i>Nightmares &amp; Dreamscapes</i>. Oh well. You know what they say. “Want in one hand and shit in the other.”<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Some of everything is eventually put on display.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18436472901056651063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8066769784316796692">The title of this story collection is deceiving, Everything's Eventual: 14 Dark Tales. Except I don't think all 14 tales were dark, in fact I think this collection had more "happy" endings then most Stephen King stories. As with all story collections there are winners and not winners with one loser(I'm looking at you The Little Sisters Of Eluria). <br/><br/>My favorites: 1)1408- is my undisputed favorite story in this collection. It lives up to all the hype its received. <br/>2) The Autopsy Room- explores one </span>
  <span id="freeText8066769784316796692" style="display:none">The title of this story collection is deceiving, Everything's Eventual: 14 Dark Tales. Except I don't think all 14 tales were dark, in fact I think this collection had more "happy" endings then most Stephen King stories. As with all story collections there are winners and not winners with one loser(I'm looking at you The Little Sisters Of Eluria). <br /><br />My favorites: 1)1408- is my undisputed favorite story in this collection. It lives up to all the hype its received. <br />2) The Autopsy Room- explores one of my biggest fears. The fear of being pronounced dead prematurely.<br /> 3) That Feeling You Can Only Say What It Is In French- I truly believe that may be what hell is. <br />4) The Road Virus Heads North- sent chills down my spine. <br /><br />Now the (Not) Favorites:1) The Man In Black- was exactly what you would think it would be. *Spoiler Alert* He's the Devil.(Yawn)<br />2) In The Deathroom-Yawn<br />3) L.T.'s Theory Of Pets- I reread it and I still missed the point<br />4) Lunch at the Gotham Cafe- Meh! <br /><br />The Worst- The Little Sisters of Eluria- it made me never want to read The Dark Tower series and it was long for no reason and pointless. <br /><br />The rest of the stories were great and probably some of them deserved to be on my favorites list. Overall I really enjoyed it and definitely recommend it to Stephen King lovers and newbies alike.<br /><br />Around The Year In 52 Books: An award winning short story or short story collection<br />Hooked On Books Read-A-Thon</span>

<div id="review_29339559" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29339559" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29339559?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29339559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12479286644181939960">I'm always amazed at how varied his subjects can be. He is certainly not "just" a horror writer.<br/><br/>05/2015<br/><br/><b>Introduction</b> 5 stars. I love King and when he is brutally honest (when is he not?) I love him all the more.<br/><br/><b>Autopsy Room 4</b> 4 stars I've actually seen the AHP episode that inspired this and Cotton was amazing. I love that only King could mention Michael Bolton and then bring up the fact that Percy is probably rolling in his grave at Bolton's rendition of "When a Man Loves a Woman". This story is </span>
  <span id="freeText12479286644181939960" style="display:none">I'm always amazed at how varied his subjects can be. He is certainly not "just" a horror writer.<br /><br />05/2015<br /><br /><b>Introduction</b> 5 stars. I love King and when he is brutally honest (when is he not?) I love him all the more.<br /><br /><b>Autopsy Room 4</b> 4 stars I've actually seen the AHP episode that inspired this and Cotton was amazing. I love that only King could mention Michael Bolton and then bring up the fact that Percy is probably rolling in his grave at Bolton's rendition of "When a Man Loves a Woman". This story is scary because...well, who knows?! It could be us, any day, any way.<br /><br /><b>The Man in Black</b> 5 stars I can't say what it is about this story that I love. I guess that's why it won awards. Who but King can say "he skun his knee" and we not only accept it, but realize how true that is? People spoke that way. He uses words to paint a world and mood and he is a master.<br /><br /><b>All the You Love will be Carried Away</b> 5 stars I know King likes to drive so I can only imagine he has actually seen all the graffiti described in the pages of this little tale. I really feel for Alfie by the end, but I think he is just the excuse King needs to get these little (weird) gems on the page.<br /><br /><b>The Death of Jack Hamilton</b> 4 stars Dillinger has always been a fascinating guy. He had charisma and that will get you so much farther in life than almost any other trait. Many say charisma was Kennedy's ace in the hole. This read to me like King testing the waters for the eventual 11/22/63. Rabbits was an endearing character and King's ability to create numerous characters we can connect to in such a limited number of pages is one of the things I love about him.<br /><br /><b>In the Deathroom</b> 4 stars This is such a novel way to end this sort of story. It reads like a scene from Scarface and yet...he gets away. There's no way to be sure it's Fletcher buying smokes at the end, but I choose to believe it <b>is</b> him.<br /><br /><b>The Little Sisters of Eluria</b> 5 stars Like many of King's fans I love Roland and his world. This story was lovely. The phrases King uses when he is in Dark Tower mode have a certain magic to them. Like he is a <i>different</i> writer when he is telling DT tales. Two quotes from this that I highlighted are "Good liars were common. Honesty, on the other hand, was dear." and as Roland ran his hands through Jenna's hair he thinks "it felt like rain, rain with weight." Both beautiful, beautiful examples of the language the Dark Tower tales insist upon. It gives me a little thrill to read the different accents/versions of the High Speech as well. "Sai" and "thee". They make you feel a part of that world, not just an observer.<br /><br /><b>Everything's Eventual</b> 5 stars More if I could! I am so glad this is the title tale of the collection. This story has always reminded me a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16165178.The_Ballad_of_the_Flexible_Bullet" title="The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ballad of the Flexible Bullet</a>. Dinky's shapes are a bit like "fornits". I am always thrilled when an author can just pull stuff out of their ass and make me not only accept, but genuinely believe in it! King does that here. I truly believe (as I read) that people can do what Dinky does, that other people can "see" the Dinkys of the world and that there could be an organization (Shop, anyone?) that would finance and set it all up. Even setting Dinky up in this mild, almost cashless existence makes sense. I want another story about a Tranny from a privileged life to see how they would deal with that. <br /><br /><b>L.T.'s Theory of Pets</b> 3 stars While I find King's musings about marriage and how it works incredibly true in this story it always leaves me unsatisfied. There is no real ending. Usually I can accept that, but for some reason I just can't in this case. Why do we need to know about L.T. breaking down, but have no clue what happens to Lulu? Why do we need to know Holly took a shine to him but not if it will lead anywhere? It does contain a great quote, though: “It might be that the biggest division in the world isn't men and women but folks who like cats and folks who like dogs" <br /><br /><b>The Road Virus Heads North</b> 3 stars I think it's fascinating that King really owns this picture, but that doesn't make the story any better for me. I think it's a bit silly.<br /><br /><b>Lunch at the Gotham Cafe</b> 4 stars I don't think the story rates the stars, but the way in which it is told does. None of what happens makes any sense and we are given no reasons which I am ok with. I do really want to know what made Diane so unhappy though. That's one question I really, really want an answer to.<br /><br /><b>That Feeling, The One You Can Only Say What it is in French</b> 2 stars King says in his note that he believes Hell may be repetition. I could not agree more. I really dislike stories that show the same scene over and over like this one. It's just so frustrating to read or watch on film. It feels like a colossal waste of time.<br /><br /><b>1408</b> 5 stars This a great story and has a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8217236.The_Yellow_Wallpaper" title="The Yellow Wallpaper by Charlotte Perkins Gilman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Yellow Wallpaper</a> feel to it. I like that King makes it very clear this is not a haunted hotel room, because haunting is done by something that was once alive, but is instead just...wrong. I also applaud his choice to allow Mike to live through the ordeal. To have him die would have felt almost cliche. I have yet to see the movie because I am afraid it won't be a fair adaptation, but I did imagine Cusak as Mike as I read this time. Perfect casting.<br /><br /><b>Riding the Bullet</b> 5 stars I've always felt this one and The Woman in the Room were about King's mother's death and he confirms that in his author's note. I love when a story is told in such a way that you can believe in the supernatural parts or not - as you choose. King gives us that choice with this little tale. <br /><br /><b>Luckey Quarter</b> 5 stars King writes in the voice of women so well, and the voice of single mothers best of all. This poor woman is doing all she can and getting jack crap for it. Such is life and this story rings so incredibly true because of it. I like to think it ends just the way her fantasy ended and King lets me think that because he doesn't say. How sweet...</span>
  <a data-text-id="12479286644181939960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1332658861" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332658861" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332658861?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=anthology-collection">anthology-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332658861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8512025685511712333">Is this collection scares, nostalgia, and downright straight-up story telling underappreciated among King’s other works? Lesser known maybe? Well, I’m here to give this one a big, sloppy ghost hug of appreciation (technically, I don’t think that’s even possible, but I’m going with it).<br/><br/>This would be my second read through of Everything’s Eventual - sort of. I used to hunt and peck through Stephen King short story collections. Read some of the stories. Skip some. No real rhyme or reason to it, unl</span>
  <span id="freeText8512025685511712333" style="display:none">Is this collection scares, nostalgia, and downright straight-up story telling underappreciated among King’s other works? Lesser known maybe? Well, I’m here to give this one a big, sloppy ghost hug of appreciation (technically, I don’t think that’s even possible, but I’m going with it).<br /><br />This would be my second read through of Everything’s Eventual - sort of. I used to hunt and peck through Stephen King short story collections. Read some of the stories. Skip some. No real rhyme or reason to it, unless someone had suggested a favorite. That’s what I did the first time around. Now I’m being thorough, and that is a good thing, especially considering the quality here. I liked so many of them. Have you read them? Well, following is a little something about each story that I hope will entice you, or perhaps refresh your memory. Get ready for hugs:<br /><br /><br /><b>Autopsy Room Four</b> - Here’s a nightmare I most certainly blocked from memory the first time around. You know the scenario: state of catatonia, everyone thinks you’re dead. So off to autopsy we go – with eyes open. And here’s another thing I never thought about before: Post-mortem shears. Maybe I’ll just block it out until the next go around.<br /><b>The Man in the Black Suit</b> - From romp (in the previous story) to introspection as Gary tells us about a day that has remained with him forever. A single day 81 years in the past could be called scary as hell. The horror at the center of this one balanced by the tender memories of a young boy make this story more than worthy of the O. Henry Award received.<br /><b>All that You Love Will Be Carried Away</b> - Beautiful title for a short story. The subject here is actually serious. Very much so. You don’t realize that, until the matter comes up. Kind of hit me like a right cross.<br /><b>The Death of Jack Hamilton</b> - I know John Dillinger of course, but figured Jack Hamilton and narrator, Homer, to be characters of fiction. There I was wrong. King says in the afterward that his dying is also a fact. Everything around it is made up. Good without excitement. No need for it. <br /><b>In the Death Room</b> - The ending is the best part of this interrogation, because as said in the afterward, it is happier than the typical.<br /><b>The Little Sisters of Eluria</b> - A Dark Tower story, any fan will enjoy because it can be read as a stand-alone, or at any point in your personal Dark Tower quest. It feels almost as if our hero Roland and Mid-World have crossed paths with Night Shift here. There was a bonus for me in reading this after just completing Black House because at one point the two books are linked - by the tiniest of threads. Good thing for Jack Sawyer that the Little Sisters have moved on, but in this one Roland has his work cut out for him.<br /><b>Everything’s Eventual</b> - The namesake to this collection is one of the best. I had no idea of its direction because no point is given until necessary. Then, it’s a kind of a doosy. I don’t know how the whole idea came from picturing a man pouring change into a sewer, but that makes it even cooler.<br /><b>L.T.’s Theory of Pets</b> - SK considers this his favorite of the bunch, but I don’t think the ending fits with the whole. The fun of story, the often true quirkiness of pets and their owners suddenly goes dark. I just don’t know why.<br /><b>The Road Virus Heads North</b> - In Rose Madder, a painting also transforms on its own. That would be the only likeness to Road Virus where the pace is much quicker and more sinister to the eye that beholds it. Rose Madder meets Christine? Not really, but that’s what I thought of.<br /><b>Lunch at the Gotham Cafe</b> - I thought this would be about divorce, then I thought it was about quitting smoking (ala Quitters, Inc.). Turns out it’s attempted murder. The characters and story are great – provided you subtract the maître d’.<br /><b>That Feeling, You Can Only Say What it is in French</b> - “Déjà vu” is what that title is saying. Carol has that feeling again and again during the drive to her and Bill’s second honeymoon, certain she knows what’s coming around the next bend. None come true – until they begin to – along with flashbacks of a past regret.<br /><b>1408</b> - Half the story has passed before you enter room 1408 with Mike. That time is spent not in building the tension, but a belief that something actually does reside in that haunted room. So when the reader finally gets there, he’s all in. It’s a different take on a ghost tale because there is no ghost to see. But something is there. Oh yeah.<br /><b>Riding the Bullet</b> - “Things have to be just right for you to see a ghost.” Tonight they were for Alan. Hitchhiking his way down state to see his mother in the hospital. Full moon. Dark roads. Just trying to get there. What makes this more than a ghost story is the nostalgia and real meaning behind it - which is about losing someone you love, and what you’d do for them in that moment. Would you ride the bullet?<br /><b>Luckey Quarter</b> - I would have liked this to end with Riding the Bullet, but in a way this smallest story of the bunch left me with a good feeling.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8512025685511712333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer483485088969192470">If I've said it once, I've said it a thousand times... and I'll say it again. Steve King is a fantastic storyteller, and very few of his stories have actually bored me. It is the same with this collection.<br/><br/>That said, very few of the stories here are actually frightening. Some give a mild sense of unease, that's all. However, almost all of them are readable and most are highly enjoyable.<br/><br/>My personal favourites were <b>That Feeling, The One You Can Only Say What it is in French</b>, <b>In the Deathroom</b> and <b>Ri</b></span>
  <span id="freeText483485088969192470" style="display:none">If I've said it once, I've said it a thousand times... and I'll say it again. Steve King is a fantastic storyteller, and very few of his stories have actually bored me. It is the same with this collection.<br /><br />That said, very few of the stories here are actually frightening. Some give a mild sense of unease, that's all. However, almost all of them are readable and most are highly enjoyable.<br /><br />My personal favourites were <b>That Feeling, The One You Can Only Say What it is in French</b>, <b>In the Deathroom</b> and <b>Riding the Bullet</b> - these were the ones which made me uneasy. The title story is fantastically original and a thumping good read. <b>The Little Sisters of Eluria</b> is a worthy addition to <i>The Dark Tower</i> canon.<br /><br />I was disappointed by <b>1408</b>, as I have seen the movie based on it and it was way more frightening than the story. <b>The Man in Black</b> and <b>Lunch at the Gotham Cafe</b> also didn't work for me.<br /><br />Overall, an enjoyable collection.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1563158565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1563158565" />
    <a title="Christian Guzman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27310486-christian-guzman"><img alt="Christian Guzman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547530878p2/27310486.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1563158565?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christian Guzman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christian Guzman" href="/user/show/27310486-christian-guzman">Christian Guzman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416552130" href="/book/show/2078360.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1563158565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12911194829491812916">There’s no doubt that Stephen King is great at writing short stories. Not all of the ones that were in this book were appealing to me, but several were. A couple of them were creepy in my opinion, so it may not be a wise idea to read them at night. My favorite ones were: Autopsy Room Four, The Man in the Black Suit, Everything’s Eventual, L.T’s Theory of Pets, and The Road Virus Heads North. I only disliked a few, but not because they were bad, they just did not catch my attention. One of the th</span>
  <span id="freeText12911194829491812916" style="display:none">There’s no doubt that Stephen King is great at writing short stories. Not all of the ones that were in this book were appealing to me, but several were. A couple of them were creepy in my opinion, so it may not be a wise idea to read them at night. My favorite ones were: Autopsy Room Four, The Man in the Black Suit, Everything’s Eventual, L.T’s Theory of Pets, and The Road Virus Heads North. I only disliked a few, but not because they were bad, they just did not catch my attention. One of the things I enjoyed was how King added notes before and after for some of the stories. For some reason that had an impact on my reading experience since it made those specific ones seem more personal. I thought the short story “1408” was average. I had watched the movie several years ago without knowing who the author was. I seemed to have enjoyed the movie more since it seemed to have gone in much more detail, so i was more engaged with the main character. There are great stories presented in this novel, and I can assure you that you will like AT LEAST one…. unless if you are a picky or difficult person to entertain. This book does not lack variety. There is a story out there for everyone! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12911194829491812916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1757821814" />
    <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen"><img alt="Daniel Clausen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603533755p2/957634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1757821814?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Clausen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Clausen" href="/user/show/957634-daniel-clausen">Daniel Clausen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757821814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer451055238223502058">Let me be clear, Mr. King. You earned this one fair and square. You had to win a skeptic over and you did. <br/><br/>I've always thought of you as the Nicholas Cage of writing. Try enough random stuff regularly without hesitation and at least some of your stuff will be pretty good. But try enough random stuff and you're sure to come up with some very bad writing as well. <br/><br/>There is also another dark secret -- some of this variability occurs in the same book. They might start off well enough, get really good</span>
  <span id="freeText451055238223502058" style="display:none">Let me be clear, Mr. King. You earned this one fair and square. You had to win a skeptic over and you did. <br /><br />I've always thought of you as the Nicholas Cage of writing. Try enough random stuff regularly without hesitation and at least some of your stuff will be pretty good. But try enough random stuff and you're sure to come up with some very bad writing as well. <br /><br />There is also another dark secret -- some of this variability occurs in the same book. They might start off well enough, get really good, then fall apart, then try to pick up the pieces, and then fall apart again. <br /><br />Much of what you write sometimes seems like a first draft. <br /><br />But for all my hesitancy to ever pick up a book by you again, I did. And it's clear --you're a great short story writer. You know how to craft compelling characters, dramatic tension, details that really sell the story and make you want to read them again. <br /><br />Not everything you wrote in this book was great. I gave up at least two short stories before finishign them. You have also cemented for me the metaphor that you're the Nick Cage of writing. But you're Nick Cageishness works wonders in the short story medium. You just go for it! Without reservation or apology. And when your short stories fall apart, I can forgive you, because I know you're just a writer working at his craft -- just going for it whenever you can. <br /><br />My experience reading this book was so good that I'm contemplating writing Nicholas Cage a letter asking him to stop acting in feature length movies and to just do two-hour features with eight to ten mini-movies. Thus, whenever he does a little mini-movie where he yells, "Aw the bees!" and flashes me strange demented grins for another ten minutes, I can forgive him and wonder, <i>Aw yes, but what's next?<i> <br /><br />And so, I leave this review wondering, Aw what will Stephen King do next? <br /><br />When I do pick up another book by you, I think it'll be a short story collection. Why not? It's like "Riding the Bullet" of fiction. Nick Cage knows what I'm talking about, "Aw the bees!" <br /><br /><br /></i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="451055238223502058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16071900832522992150">SK can't help being SK. That includes profanity and poor taste. Often, it seems like it's trying fine cuisine at Denney's. Every once in a while, you'll find something that tastes excellent.   <span id="freeText16071900832522992150" style="display:none">SK can't help being SK. That includes profanity and poor taste. Often, it seems like it's trying fine cuisine at Denney's. Every once in a while, you'll find something that tastes excellent. Mostly it'll be when you are famished.<br /><br />Month after month and year after year, he churns it out, and he has for decades and decades now. I read this collection of horror stories after the members of my reading group--mostly women--caved in to the only other male in the group besides me. Many of the women had never read King, and said it was time to give him a try. Many swore him off after reading the collection, claiming there is just too much good to read without having to touch his stuff.<br /><br />I beg to differ. SK is probably the greatest commercial writer of my generation. He speaks to the masses, to our crassnesses and to the mysterious in us as human beings, wich we love to morph into ever-increaing weirdness.<br /><br />Hence, SK, for example, conceives a snake-bitten cadaver "resurrected" during an autopsy when, well, when a doctor, a woman, about to slice into him, discovers---no, I'll yet you read about its swelling fervor. Or what about the guy who has spent a career as a traveling salesman who has collected the detritus scrawled on the walls of toilet walls and stalls across the countryside in a note book, planning to publish who now wants to shoot---what, you thought I'd tell you?<br /><br />No, no . . . I recommend that you read it yourself, and see what you think. Why has this American icon found so much success writing about the dark and fearful in American history and culture.<br /><br />If you don't appreciate horror, read his <i>On Writing</i> and <i>The Girl Who Loved Tom Gordon</i>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7063488151797242732"> I kept picking this up & reading a tale or two at a time. Each time I did this, I was struck by the way in which King brings a certain quality to his writing that just plain makes him better than most. He brings a certain assumption of the intelligence of his readers and gives us credit for being able to pick up the dark humor, the allusions, and the ironies he weaves. He has a unique ability to construct setting and characters so quickly and seamlessly that we have an instant picture in our mi</span>
  <span id="freeText7063488151797242732" style="display:none"> I kept picking this up &amp; reading a tale or two at a time. Each time I did this, I was struck by the way in which King brings a certain quality to his writing that just plain makes him better than most. He brings a certain assumption of the intelligence of his readers and gives us credit for being able to pick up the dark humor, the allusions, and the ironies he weaves. He has a unique ability to construct setting and characters so quickly and seamlessly that we have an instant picture in our mind and an opinion beginning to form. All within the limits of a short story with nothing sacrificed. <br />Whether or not one likes his subject matter, King is a master wordsmith with the wonderful quality of not taking himself too seriously. He takes his writing seriously, but there is no pretension in his work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7063488151797242732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review99867429">

<div id="review_1256579357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256579357" />
    <a title="Jaro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41513821-jaro"><img alt="Jaro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596355784p2/41513821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1256579357?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaro" href="/user/show/41513821-jaro">Jaro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780340770733" href="/book/show/912842.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41513821-jaro?shelf=p-stephen-king-read">p-stephen-king-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41513821-jaro?shelf=work">work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41513821-jaro?shelf=t-painting">t-painting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256579357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11977876349324108722">A strong collections of stories. I liked it better than both Bazaar and Sunset. King has such a firm grasp on the Voice and Tone of his characters. My favorites were those stories told in the first person: "The Man in the Black Suit", "Everything's Eventual", "Lunch at the Gotham Café", and "Riding the Bullet". I was surprised by "The Little Sisters of Eluria" which has a sort of sword and sorcery feel to it that I really liked.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_621452531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621452531" />
    <a title="Jonathan Janz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4415785-jonathan-janz"><img alt="Jonathan Janz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518203259p2/4415785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621452531?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Janz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Janz" href="/user/show/4415785-jonathan-janz">Jonathan Janz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621452531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9903201058972330228">*This review was originally published on my blog (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://jonathanjanz.com'>http://jonathanjanz.com</a>) and focuses on the story "The Road Virus Heads North" (though I've read the whole collection and certainly believe it's worthy of five stars). Here's the link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://jonathanjanz.com/2011/10/08/the-road-virus-heads-north/'>http://jonathanjanz.com/2011/10/08/th...</a> ‎<br/><br/>Stephen King's Everything's Eventual is loaded with great stories. In addition to the one I'm about to discuss, the collection contains "1408," "Lunch at the Gotham Cafe," and a cool entry into the Dark Tower canon called "</span>
  <span id="freeText9903201058972330228" style="display:none">*This review was originally published on my blog (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jonathanjanz.com">http://jonathanjanz.com</a>) and focuses on the story "The Road Virus Heads North" (though I've read the whole collection and certainly believe it's worthy of five stars). Here's the link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jonathanjanz.com/2011/10/08/the-road-virus-heads-north/">http://jonathanjanz.com/2011/10/08/th...</a> ‎<br /><br />Stephen King's Everything's Eventual is loaded with great stories. In addition to the one I'm about to discuss, the collection contains "1408," "Lunch at the Gotham Cafe," and a cool entry into the Dark Tower canon called "The Little Sisters of Eluria."<br /><br />So in a collection packed with great stories, why'd I choose to blog about "Virus"?<br /><br />Let me try to explain...<br /><br />First of all, like Stephen King---and I'll shamelessly seize any opportunity to be like my favorite writer ever---I love stories about pictures. Specifically, I love stories about pictures that change. King has worked in this shadowy corner before, notably in "The Sun Dog," and it's a territory into which other great authors (T.E.D. Klein's unforgettable novella "Petey" comes to mind) have ventured as well. So is this tale King's most original?<br /><br />I don't give a crap. Sure, sometimes it's dazzling to find an author blazing a completely new trail, but for me it's just as exciting to see a master take a tattered old idea and breathe new life into it.<br /><br />Like "The Road Virus Heads North."<br /><br />It's about a horror author who finds a rather...arresting painting at a garage sale. The painting has a macabre backstory that I don't want to ruin here, but as we'd expect from a horror author (a bizarre species prone to excessive curiosity), he purchases the piece and continues, well, north.<br /><br />The name Richard Kinnell reminds me of both Richard Bachman (King's pseudonym) and Dr. Richard Kimble of The Fugitive fame; whether or not either of these connections are intentional, they both add texture to the character for me. I don't want to give away what happens in this story, but if you've been reading, you'll already know that the painting changes. How it changes and where it changes and how Richard reacts to these changes and what these changes mean for Richard and those with whom he comes into contact...all of these are what make the tale so elegant and ghastly.<br /><br />As has been pointed out by people far smarter than I, horror is the only genre named after an emotion (although I felt a bit "men's adventury" today when I attempted to parallel park in a space two inches longer than my car). That's because horror can affect the reader in a very unique way. And man, did this tale affect me. I felt dread when the first layers of the mystery peeled away to reveal just how sinister the painting might be. I felt terror when Richard Kinnell realized that the picture could defy physics and reason. And I felt horror during those last few pages when...<br /><br />Read the story. It's a darn good one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9903201058972330228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
