<div id="review_3247374997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3247374997" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3247374997?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=short-fiction">short-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3247374997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17537738387558731410">Averaging the individual stories, 3.75 stars for the collection as a whole.<br/><br/>This wasn't my favourite short story collection by King. I recently read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23512999.The_Bazaar_of_Bad_Dreams' title='The Bazaar of Bad Dreams by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bazaar of Bad Dreams</a>, which I felt had a certain cohesiveness as a group of stories that Everything's Eventual, while still good, lacked. <br/><br/>That said, there were some great stories in this. I read this with a group, and interestingly, the stories that appealed to me the most - <i>The Death of Jack Hamilton, Everything's Eventual, </i>and <i>Riding the Bullet</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17537738387558731410" style="display:none">Averaging the individual stories, 3.75 stars for the collection as a whole.<br /><br />This wasn't my favourite short story collection by King. I recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23512999.The_Bazaar_of_Bad_Dreams" title="The Bazaar of Bad Dreams by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bazaar of Bad Dreams</a>, which I felt had a certain cohesiveness as a group of stories that Everything's Eventual, while still good, lacked. <br /><br />That said, there were some great stories in this. I read this with a group, and interestingly, the stories that appealed to me the most - <i>The Death of Jack Hamilton, Everything's Eventual, </i>and <i>Riding the Bullet </i>- were not the ones favoured by the majority. What I like about King, what he demonstrates in the stories that affect me the most, is his ability to capture character and place them effectively with horror elements. <br /><br />The thing about horror, though, is that it doesn't necessarily mean gore or jump scares. It can, of course, but true horror encompasses as larger and more subtle range of discomfortable feelings such as loss, vague fear, and creeping existential dread. For me, King succeeds most when he uses the range of our human discomfort in the telling of a story, and pairs that with what we know and love. It is that juxtaposition that provides suspense, investment, and the eventual emotional payoff in learning the fate of an individual character or outcome of a story. That is what I look for, and that is where my ratings for each story come from. Overall, there were some pretty good ones in here, and a few misses (for me) too.<br /><br /><b>Autopsy Room Four (4/5)</b> - The conceit of being alive yet mistaken for dead is classic for a reason. It's something everyone can imagine for themselves and be equally horrified by.<br /><br />This was a very good start to set the tone. I honestly didn't know what was going to happen. Things can go either way with King.<br /><br /><b>The Man in the Black Suit (4/5)</b> - This O. Henry Prize winner uses another classic set up, with an elderly man finally relating the tale of a youthful encounter with the Devil. The protagonist has a wonderfully flowing and effecting voice in the telling of his story, bringing the incident fully to life.<br /><br />It is interesting that King calls this one of those stories that he felt compelled to tell. That same sense of compulsion runs through the text. There is an urgency in the man to unburden himself of this secret held for scores of years, underlaid with his admitted fear that he may yet see the Devil again. Since innocence did not help him as a child, there is no reason to think living a good life as an adult will be enough to protect him from a final visit.<br /><br /><b>All That You Love Will Be Carried Away (4/5)</b> A snapshot type story where you get an intensely personal look at a travelling salesman, and slowly come to understand what is going on with him. I love the setting of the chain motel off the Interstate, with the surrounding field and wind intensifying the competing senses of closeness and isolation. The ambiguous ending fits the piece perfectly.<br /><br /><b>The Death of Jack Hamilton (4.5/5)</b> In the audiobook version this story is perfectly narrated by Arliss Howard. He has an intelligent yet accessible lilt to his voice that sets the stage perfectly for this Depression era tale of the outlaw Dillinger gang trying to deal with the injury and slow death of a beloved member. By turns shocking, funny, sad, and sometimes grotesque, it is in all ways memorable.<br /><br /><b>In the Deathroom (2.5/5)</b> I didn't much care for this one, only because I felt like it was a familiar premise (drug cartel interrogation) and there wasn't enough of a twist to make it stand out from similar stories, film, and TV scenes.<br /><br /><b>The Little Sisters of Eluria (3/5)</b> This is a prequel story to The Dark Tower series, which I haven't read. The interesting genre-crossover feel of the piece gives a fresh twist to the vampiric monster tale. Appropriate levels of dread are also brought to bear by the use of insects which apparently operate under the direction of the Sisters.<br /><br /><b>Everything's Eventual (4.5/5)</b> This story is one of my favourite kind of horror stories; where things start out seeming ok and ordinary and then start to reveal the darker side of what is happening. It reminds me of the kinds of stories from The Twilight Zone, or more recently, Black Mirror. Again, the slightly open end added to the chill.<br /><br /><b>L.T.'s Theory of Pets (4/5)</b> Another story where I felt like I got to know the narrator well through his storytelling. It's a story that is at first about a marriage breaking up and then it becomes clear that the telling and retelling of the story is really more a form of denial.<br /><br /><b>The Road Virus Heads North (4/5)</b> More of a classic feeling King-style horror. Right from the start you know where it's going, but you can't do anything to stop it.<br /><br /><b>Lunch at the Gotham Cafe (4/5)</b>Another study in how normal life can shift suddenly, and violently. I liked the use of misdirection in terms of where that violence comes from, although the ending makes you wonder whether it was misdirection or simply foreshadowing?<br /><br /><b>That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is In French (3/5)</b> Loop stories are hit or miss for me. I didn't love this one, but it did have some interesting elements.<br /><br /><b>1408 (3/5)</b> The obligatory haunting story, as King calls it. It was ok, and definitely creepy, but everything unfolded pretty much in the way I expected, so the emotional payoff was a bit lacking. That said, this seems to be the kind of straightforward horror lots of people say they read King for. <br /><br /><b>Riding the Bullet (4/5)</b><br />A suspenseful story about impossible choices and confronting mortality. The strong horror elements are an excellent setting for the characters, who seem very real and lifelike.<br /><br /><b>Luckey Quarter (4/5)</b><br />There is something really charming about this story. It captures perfectly that sense that so many mothers have of never being able to quite do enough, but just pushing through day to day as best you can. I hope the luck held.<br /><br /><b>Notes on the audiobook:</b> I did a combination of audio and print when reading this. There is a different narrator for each story, and mostly they were pretty good. My favourite was definitely Arliss Howard reading <i>The Death of Jack Hamilton</i>. My only real complaint is that the audiobook contains neither the introduction nor the text by the author that introduces or ends each story. To me that is a pretty grave oversight as these things are part of what makes this a collection rather than a bunch of individual stories. If you do listen to the audiobook, I recommend checking the print copy for the extra text, which is always interesting and relevant to the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17537738387558731410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_28670354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28670354" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28670354?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780743457354" href="/book/show/559298.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=shortstories-collections">shortstories-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28670354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7109600144885316599">Yet another example of why I love Stephen King. Every story in this book was great. King's ability to write like he's speaking only to YOU is one of my favorite things about him. You get the feeling that he's telling you a secret, letting you in on some amazing observation of life, without him needing to spell every D-E-T-A-I-L out in big bold block letters. But that's not to say that this isn't detailed - his work always is. It's just not condescendingly detailed. You may think that he is verbo</span>
  <span id="freeText7109600144885316599" style="display:none">Yet another example of why I love Stephen King. Every story in this book was great. King's ability to write like he's speaking only to YOU is one of my favorite things about him. You get the feeling that he's telling you a secret, letting you in on some amazing observation of life, without him needing to spell every D-E-T-A-I-L out in big bold block letters. But that's not to say that this isn't detailed - his work always is. It's just not condescendingly detailed. You may think that he is verbose, and in some cases I'd agree, but he never condescends to his readers, and trusts that we are smart enough to see what he's aiming at without having to hold our hands. <br /><br />Some of these stories are more straightforward than others, but some are brilliantly subtle. It's hard for me to decide which one is my favorite, but after giving it some thought, I think that I'd have to say it's <b>"That Feeling, You Can Only Say What It Is In French"</b>. This story is short, only 24 pages, but I was impressed by just how much was conveyed in such a small amount of words. So much history, so much regret and satisfaction and fear and anger, so much expectation and irritation. You could almost feel what it was like for this couple to have been married for 25 years... and then on top of that, there's Carol's deja vu, and the fear associated with that, which is a different type of fear entirely. I loved the way that with each run-through we learn more about what's causing the deja vu, and I thought it was brilliant. I've had deja vu before, I think everyone has, and while Carol recognized it and was able to live within it and even almost predict the things that would come next, my experience has been that it's a fleeting moment of disorienting recognition that I only realize I've felt after it's already gone. I can only hope that I never have the experience it the way that Carol did. <br /><br />I loved the two stories that were tied to the Dark Tower series, <b>"The Little Sisters of Eluria"</b> and <b>"Everything's Eventual"</b>. Both of these stories tie wonderfully into the Dark Tower universe and provide more background and depth and life to the story as a whole. Of the two, I actually preferred the more subtle <b>"Everything's Eventual"</b>, but I loved both. I just loved the way that we never really know what's going on with Dinky, what he's gotten himself into, but we know it's bad, and that where it leads, eventually, is worse, for him and for us. Little Sisters is great though, and seeing Roland again was a little bit like meeting up with an old friend that you haven't seen in many years. This story provides a bit of background into both Roland and his world, and when taken in context with The Gunslinger, proves that Roland is nothing if not unpredictable. <br /><br />Also very high on my list is <b>"All That You Love Will Be Carried Away"</b>, which is a brilliant story about the little things that get us through, that fascinate us and make us want to keep going more than the big things.<br /><br />I very much enjoyed <b>"LT's Theory Of Pets"</b>. One should not look at a living creature as a gift to be given, because they cannot be owned. They have thoughts and feelings and desires and needs just like the rest of us, they just can't communicate them as we can. But this is also a story of the breakdown of a marriage and how quickly things can go badly when a single (OK, two) peas are placed under the mattress. What we do in love and the desire to please can have quite unexpected consequences.<br /><br />I liked each of the stories in this book, but I have to say that these were my favorites. I would definitely recommend this to someone looking for some great stories, King fan or not. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7109600144885316599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16054986547124789475">There are no bad stories in this collection. Love it.<br/><br/>“Autopsy Room Four” – Super creepy and I love the ending. Four stars.<br/><br/>“The Man in the Black Suit” – Somewhat less definitive than I would have liked, but the descriptions are amazing.   <span id="freeText16054986547124789475" style="display:none">There are no bad stories in this collection. Love it.<br /><br />“Autopsy Room Four” – Super creepy and I love the ending. Four stars.<br /><br />“The Man in the Black Suit” – Somewhat less definitive than I would have liked, but the descriptions are amazing. Three stars.<br /><br />“All That You Love Will Be Carried Away” - The lady or the tiger? Four stars.<br /><br />“The Death of Jack Hamilton” – This was so sad, and also disgusting. <div id="review_2013895585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2013895585" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24154009-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578362761p2/24154009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2013895585?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/24154009-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743235150" href="/book/show/644172.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24154009-jason?shelf=short-story-collections">short-story-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24154009-jason?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2013895585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1972293985432778457">Some good, some mediocre. This isn't my favourite collection of short stories from Stephen King (I've enjoyed Bazaar of Bad Dreams the most so far, which probably doesn't make me in the majority). <br/><br/>What I disliked about the some of these stories is that King uses the word "short" almost as a joke in this collection. Some of these are 40 or 50 pages, and are pretty well novellas. Even King says short stories are meant to be read in one sitting, but some of them took two or three for me - probably </span>
  <span id="freeText1972293985432778457" style="display:none">Some good, some mediocre. This isn't my favourite collection of short stories from Stephen King (I've enjoyed Bazaar of Bad Dreams the most so far, which probably doesn't make me in the majority). <br /><br />What I disliked about the some of these stories is that King uses the word "short" almost as a joke in this collection. Some of these are 40 or 50 pages, and are pretty well novellas. Even King says short stories are meant to be read in one sitting, but some of them took two or three for me - probably I'm just a slow reader. I do, however, feel that a short story is becoming too long when it exceeds the 30 page mark. <br /><br />That said, there were a few notable stories in here that I really enjoyed:<br />- Autopsy Room Four<br />- All That You Love Will Be Carried Away<br />- L.T.'s Theory of Pets<br />- Lunch at the Gotham Café<br />- Riding the Bullet<br />- Lucky Quarter<br /><br />Give the way the novel is marketed (the cover, namely, and the "14 Dark Tales" message on the cover) I figured these would be more scary. But there were only one or two that I found might be considered a "Dark Tale." Most, though, were just regular old stories, which didn't make them bad stories, but sort of left me disappointed in the end. I wanted more punch from them, more of a slap in the face, eye-opening conclusion to each.<br /><br />Mostly, my own expectations probably ruined the overall experience, given that I was expecting more horror and terror. And I should know better, by now, that King tend to write longer stories (short stories included) than your average author might. <br /><br />On to the next King! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1972293985432778457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3234490813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3234490813" />
    <a title="L.S. Popovich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4567704-l-s-popovich"><img alt="L.S. Popovich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537455199p2/4567704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3234490813?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L.S. Popovich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L.S. Popovich" href="/user/show/4567704-l-s-popovich">L.S. Popovich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=magic-realism">magic-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=audiobook-greats">audiobook-greats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4567704-l-s-popovich?shelf=american">american</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3234490813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15234540695957375565">Once a year or so I will listen to an audiobook of one of Stephen King's novels or collections, usually without much enthusiasm. Occasionally I'll skip ahead or abandon one of them in the middle. For this collection, I experienced more mixed feelings. The title story and a few of the others were great. Genuinely well-written, riveting and so forth, but I was not much interested in the majority of them, which ranged from passable to unacceptable in my opinion. I could write a huge list of literar</span>
  <span id="freeText15234540695957375565" style="display:none">Once a year or so I will listen to an audiobook of one of Stephen King's novels or collections, usually without much enthusiasm. Occasionally I'll skip ahead or abandon one of them in the middle. For this collection, I experienced more mixed feelings. The title story and a few of the others were great. Genuinely well-written, riveting and so forth, but I was not much interested in the majority of them, which ranged from passable to unacceptable in my opinion. I could write a huge list of literary misdemeanors he might or might not have committed, but instead, I think it is valuable to look at what he accomplishes with his good stories.<br /><br />Time is often slowed down to a crawl. His narrators will observe an often tragic event in microscopic detail. The autopsy story was done in this mode. I will say it was an effective story, and opened the collection well enough, but I found myself wishing I could take a red editor's pencil and strike out every third line. Tighter editing would have benefited several of the stories IMHO. The second story was nearly flawless. A well-composed, restrained character study and an examination of that border between reality and the underground irreality we all encounter at some point or another.<br /><br />There was a gunslinger story, on par with the rest of the series, but not quite essential overall.<br />Then "Everything's Eventual" really got me. Some of his best stories are not horror. When he relies on blood and guts many of his deeper themes take a back seat. I'm thinking of Needful Things and Duma Key. His best novel I've read so far is Lisey's Story, which King claimed at one point in his career to be his best, though not his favorite.<br /><br />From my perspective, King's work appears to be a 45,000-page internal monologue spewed across various outrageous and tangentially connected scenarios with recurrent supernatural events cropping up among the same set of stock characters. That is not to say there is no variety or interest to be found. I find myself returning frequently to his work, more so than Dan Simmons or some of the other writers I have never found a love for. Most of the time, he has a solid hook, and pulls off the beginning of a story or a novel with aplomb. <br /><br />I know this collection will satisfy King fans and it shouldn't offend casual pretend-fans like me. It's worth a listen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15234540695957375565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2004726034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004726034" />
    <a title="WarpDrive" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16160897-warpdrive"><img alt="WarpDrive" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605312701p2/16160897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004726034?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WarpDrive" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WarpDrive" href="/user/show/16160897-warpdrive">WarpDrive</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340770740" href="/book/show/68949.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16160897-warpdrive?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004726034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12314186859262072255">Well, the author does not need much of an introduction. He has a gift for generating a sense of deep unease, and for awakening in the reader's mind some hidden, almost ancestral fears deeply embedded into his/her consciousness. His exploration of the darker side of human nature, and his atmospheric tales that well transcend the limitations of the "horror" genre, are reminiscent of the work of one of my favourite authors, Edgar Allan Poe.<br/>This is a collection of short stories, some of them <i>(such a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12314186859262072255" style="display:none">Well, the author does not need much of an introduction. He has a gift for generating a sense of deep unease, and for awakening in the reader's mind some hidden, almost ancestral fears deeply embedded into his/her consciousness. His exploration of the darker side of human nature, and his atmospheric tales that well transcend the limitations of the "horror" genre, are reminiscent of the work of one of my favourite authors, Edgar Allan Poe.<br />This is a collection of short stories, some of them <i>(such as "Autopsy Room Four", "The Man in the Black Suit", "All that you love will be carried away, and "1408"</i>) are pure brilliance, the Stephen King we are used to.<br />Being a collection of several stories, not all of them are equally brilliant, of course, and a few are quite forgettable, to be honest, but overall this is quite an enjoyable reading experience. 4 stars.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12314186859262072255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123534212?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743235150" href="/book/show/644172.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=horror-suspense">horror-suspense</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123534212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4149880664737648850">I haven't read much King, this is actually only the second book I've read by him (the first being Gunslinger). I've always wanted to get into him though, and I think this was the perfect book to start with. Fourteen short stories, a King smorgasbord, so to speak. Some I loved, some I just liked, some just weren't my thing - but overall it was a great collection. Every one was well written, and even if a story wasn't my favorite, I still found myself enjoying it. Highly recommended, and I'll defi</span>
  <span id="freeText4149880664737648850" style="display:none">I haven't read much King, this is actually only the second book I've read by him (the first being Gunslinger). I've always wanted to get into him though, and I think this was the perfect book to start with. Fourteen short stories, a King smorgasbord, so to speak. Some I loved, some I just liked, some just weren't my thing - but overall it was a great collection. Every one was well written, and even if a story wasn't my favorite, I still found myself enjoying it. Highly recommended, and I'll definitely be reading more King soon.</span>

<div id="review_1917882415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917882415" />
    <a title="Damien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5565551-damien"><img alt="Damien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483508104p2/5565551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917882415?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damien" href="/user/show/5565551-damien">Damien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416549857" href="/book/show/713989.Everything_s_Eventual">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917882415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2688004905167445176">It's always difficult to review a collection of short stories and this one is no exception. For the most part I thought it was a great collection of work but I did struggle a little to see a thread through these stories - was I looking for something not there or miss it completely?<br/><br/>For Dark Tower fans and for those other kinds of people, those that haven't read The Dark Tower yet, The Little Sisters of Eluria is a treat. The titular Everything's Eventual is great creepy fun and L.T.'s Theory of P</span>
  <span id="freeText2688004905167445176" style="display:none">It's always difficult to review a collection of short stories and this one is no exception. For the most part I thought it was a great collection of work but I did struggle a little to see a thread through these stories - was I looking for something not there or miss it completely?<br /><br />For Dark Tower fans and for those other kinds of people, those that haven't read The Dark Tower yet, The Little Sisters of Eluria is a treat. The titular Everything's Eventual is great creepy fun and L.T.'s Theory of Pets shows a surprisingly funny side to King's writing, who knew?<br /><br />The only stories of the fourteen that didn't really work for me were The Death of Jack Hamilton and In the Death Room. Ironically I felt they were essentially the same story with only the setting changed.<br /><br />The Man in the Black Suit is creepy fun but I was surprised to see it was the recipient of the O. Henry award.<br /><br />Overall lot's of fun in bite-sized chunks. As someone who is working on short stories at the moment, it's great to see someone in King's position take the time to continue to produce these stories and show the rest of us how it is done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2688004905167445176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bW64ywf9EJW/rMrDjLwnqtWaHTTRhVLY1Mo9RJrzhD9M6RdqCFCQYKzzjyYuyybKO62/2na2sZ7sLeyVgsspVw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lBPlQipS55J86F8BaYTdZ1HglGSEa3GNMVUbvH/4niG1lErjJf9nZ2+3GuTL89wHv9c2iiNYkssJssptZ8AzSQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14673515332224007348">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText14673515332224007348" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14673515332224007348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
